A JSTree version of my Perl.Wiki

CPAN::MetaCurator V 1.21. 2026-05-31T12:47:26

My home page, for downloading Perl.Wiki.html

Notes:
⊕ Nodes just under the root ('MetaCurator') are called Topics. Paragraphs is the TiddlyWiki equivalent.
⊕ Tokens like [[XS]] indicate a TiddlyWiki paragraph name, not a Perl module or topic.
⊕ Almost all leaf node are links. Use a middle-button click to open the link in another tab.
⊕ The code does not yet cleanly handle special cases such as the FAQ.

⊕ My other module, CPAN::MetaPackages, builds & ships an SQLite db containing 02packages.details.txt.
⊕ Most recent version of 02packages.details.txt used: .
⊕ Acronyms: 0. Known modules: 0. Leaves: 6354. Topics: 207. Unknown modules: 0

      • FAQ
        • See also - CPAN.
        • - https://www.defectivebydesign.org.
        • - What guides are included in this wiki?.
        • - TheLanguageGuide.
        • - How do I handle escaping & quoting of special characters?.
        • Where can I get an overview of internet terminology? - https://graphcomp.com/info/glossary.html.
        • - A copy of this file is at http://savage.net.au/misc/AI_POLICY.md.
        • - Why are AI agents so dangerous.
        • - What modules ship with Perl?.
        • What does deprecated mean? - It means the module's maintainer says the module is no longer suitable for use.
        • - Where are deprecated & discouraged modules discussed?.
        • What is Corinna? - https://ovid.github.io/articles/corinna-in-the-perl-core.html.
        • - Some are oriented to specific problems, whereas others are based on a different way of thinking. Typically, the latter are event-based, not data-based, so they react to things like start tag, end tag, etc. It all depends on how you think about your problem, and your specific requirements.
        • - How to understand scalar context 'v' list context?.
        • How to understand reusable regxps? - https://dev.to/damil/beautiful-perl-feature-reusable-subregexes-4iib.
        • - https://metacpan.org/pod/HTML::Tree::AboutObjects - For the article: "User's View of Object-Oriented Modules".
        • - Where do I find info on iterators?.
        • Why don't you include Catalyst, Dancer, Moose, etc? - My time is limited..
        • What is prompt injection - It is semantic mimicry: adversarial instructions that resemble legitimate prompts, which trigger self-compromise.
        • - pre>.
        • Why is prompt injection dangerous - LLMs process token sequences, but no mechanism exists to mark token privileges. The LLM can't tell the difference between legitimate input and corrupt input, so can be tricked into giving the latter priority. This might make it unsolvable in todayâs LLMs.
        • What specifically is the problem with prompt injection - In training, we face poisoned datasets and backdoored models. In inference, we face adversarial inputs and prompt injection. During operation, we face a contaminated context and persistent compromise. We need semantic integrity: verifying not just data but interpretation, not just content but context, not just information but understanding. We can add checksums, signatures, and audit logs. But how do you checksum a thought? How do you sign semantics? How do you audit attention?.

        • See also - WikiStuff.
        • - https://foswiki.org/Home/About - For FosWiki, a collaboration tool.
        • Escape character for '/' is '#&47;'. See also /''''/ and '////'. Click edit (pencil) to examine - Care! TiddlyWikis contains executable code in order to provide all the features listed below.
        • Overview - Each TiddlyWiki is restricted to a single web page.
        • - These guidelines help people with no expertise in data collation to index items carefully.
        • - Inbuilt features of all TiddlyWikis.
        • - The 3 double-quotes at the top of this para is one such command, but they are only visible when you click the pencil (edit) icon to enter edit mode for a para.
        • - Import capability (a way of sharing).
        • On-line help - See tiddlywiki.com for a free download and many add-ons from the eco-system.
        • - In the eco-system there are various public hosting options giving other ways to share besides the import feature mentioned above.

      • ZMQ
        • See also - FileHandling - for FFI::*.
        • - found ZeroMQ to be a lot of effort to use from Perl, and most critically it does not appear to support both request/response and publish/subscribe message flows to share the same UNIX socket. To support that in ZeroMQ it would appear to be necessary to create two separate endpoints, one for each kind of message flow..
